<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16290997839670698635">Heavy Snow...Icy Desires...Cold-Blooded Murder<br /><br />Clare Fergusson, St. Alban's new priest, fits like a square peg in the conservative Episcopal parish at Millers Kill, New York. She is not just a "lady," she's a tough ex-Army chopper pilot, and nobody's fool. Then a newborn infant left at the church door brings her together with the town's police chief, Russ Van Alstyne, who's</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16290997839670698635">Heavy Snow...Icy Desires...Cold-Blooded Murder<br /><br />Clare Fergusson, St. Alban's new priest, fits like a square peg in the conservative Episcopal parish at Millers Kill, New York. She is not just a "lady," she's a tough ex-Army chopper pilot, and nobody's fool. Then a newborn infant left at the church door brings her together with the town's police chief, Russ Van Alstyne, who's also ex-Army and a cynical good shepherd for the stray sheep of his hometown. Their search for the baby's mother quickly leads them into the secrets that shadow Millers Kill like the ever-present Adirondacks. What they discover is a world of trouble, an attraction to each other—and murder...<br /><br /><em>In the Bleak Midwinter</em> was Julia Spencer-Fleming's first novel, and it won a Macavity Award, an Agatha Award, an Anthony Award, and a Dilys Award.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16290997839670698635">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_164706198">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164706198" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3373844-diana" class="left imgcol" title="Diana"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1357870902p2/3373844.jpg" alt="Diana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/164706198?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 04, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3373844-diana" class="user" title="Diana">Diana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3373844-diana?shelf=audiobooks" class="actionLinkLite">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer164706198">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6306825195624818709">The mystery is the only reason I finished the book. I did not like Clare, I did not like Russ, I did not like the narrator. That pretty much sums it up. Knowing that many people whose opinions I respect adore this series and being aware of its awards, I have to just scratch my head and say "but not for me."<br /><br />As other less than favorable reviews have noted, the premise is fatally flawed. The author tells me that Clare is a smart, competent war veteran while showing me a wacky meddler with a dangero</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6306825195624818709">The mystery is the only reason I finished the book. I did not like Clare, I did not like Russ, I did not like the narrator. That pretty much sums it up. Knowing that many people whose opinions I respect adore this series and being aware of its awards, I have to just scratch my head and say "but not for me."<br /><br />As other less than favorable reviews have noted, the premise is fatally flawed. The author tells me that Clare is a smart, competent war veteran while showing me a wacky meddler with a dangerously low level of impulse control. She blurts out what she should keep in confidence and hares off into peril...repeatedly. And she's smug and self-righteous.<br /><br />Russ is at best a barely competent police chief. He allows Clare to take over his murder investigation. Why? I dunno.<br /><br />I'm puzzled as to why so many romance readers embrace Clare and Russ. He is married to a woman who is no more than an annoying stick figure and who remains conveniently out of town. Her unworthiness is explained as an overindulgence in window treatments and that she wants to start her own business. Oh, the horror. Clare careens from one TSTL moment to another, always unprepared and laughably underdressed for the bleak midwinter weather.<br /><br />Both Clare and Russ are old enough and experienced enough to grasp the fact that they're playing with fire, yet they're blindsided and outraged when the inevitable small town gossip starts. Hello?<br /><br />Cap off all this with a narrator whose Virginia drawl is a mile off base and who reads Russ in weird Daffy Duck voice, and I'm done.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6306825195624818709">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer219297881">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5958979187052875919">I am an avaricious consumer of mystery series, but there are so many stand-alone books that I want and need to read right now that yet another delectable series is an unwise choice. Well, too late. I read the first in the Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne, In the Bleak Midwinter, and once again, I'm hooked. Julia Spencer-Fleming is another Bouchercon 2013 author that I wanted to sample before the September gathering, and I duped myself into believing that I could indeed eat just one. I will begin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5958979187052875919">I am an avaricious consumer of mystery series, but there are so many stand-alone books that I want and need to read right now that yet another delectable series is an unwise choice. Well, too late. I read the first in the Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne, In the Bleak Midwinter, and once again, I'm hooked. Julia Spencer-Fleming is another Bouchercon 2013 author that I wanted to sample before the September gathering, and I duped myself into believing that I could indeed eat just one. I will begin #2 today. <br /><br />This series, set in the shadows of the Adirondack mountains in the small town of Millers Kill, features ex-Amy helicopter pilot, newly ordained Episcopalian priest Clare Fergusson and ex-Army, present-day police chief Russ Van Alstyne. Clare is the first female priest at the Episcopal church in Millers Kill, and is quite different than her conventional predecessor. When only after a month on the job, she discovers a newborn baby abandoned outside the church, Clare quickly becomes involved in the search for its parents and the subsequent murder of the baby's mother. As rapid as her involvement in the resolution to these mysteries and ones to follow, her friendship with Russ Van Alstyne, the chief of police, takes the fast trak to closeness and trusted confidant. Of course, the chief is married, which creates a stumbling block to a more intimate relationship. In solving not one, but two murders, Clare and Russ come to rely on one another's intelligence and intuition, moving in sync as two partners with different skills that mirror in a complimentary efficiency. <br /><br />It's always so satisfying to encounter yet another author whose manipulation of the language results in a spine-tingling tale. Julia Spencer-Fleming is extraordinarily gifted in her skill of description, including settiing, action, and characters. I was truly amazed at the detail of description in those areas, and it made the story so complete. There is no fuzzy, half-hearted imagery in Ms. Spencer-Fleming's writing. The reader is treated to complete disclosure of what a place looks like, what a character's physical and emotional make-up is, and what the action would look like if you were there. The twists and turns of the plot are page-turning pleasures. Now, on to the next adventure/mystery of the Clare and Russ team. Again, my reading pile groans with the weight of of books waiting. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5958979187052875919">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/98395-red?shelf=kindle-books" class="actionLinkLite">kindle-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46344612">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2533964733034641219">This book was a good beach book, perfect to read on a hot summer day because it takes place in a very cold New England winter.<br /><br />I'm not a huge mystery reader, but I enjoyed this book. I liked the police character, I liked the amateur sleuth, I liked the small town, I liked the supporting characters, and I didn't figure out who done it ahead of time. Our protagonist, Claire, is an Episcopalian priest, who in her previous career was an Army chopper pilot. The police chief is your basic rugged New En</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2533964733034641219">This book was a good beach book, perfect to read on a hot summer day because it takes place in a very cold New England winter.<br /><br />I'm not a huge mystery reader, but I enjoyed this book. I liked the police character, I liked the amateur sleuth, I liked the small town, I liked the supporting characters, and I didn't figure out who done it ahead of time. Our protagonist, Claire, is an Episcopalian priest, who in her previous career was an Army chopper pilot. The police chief is your basic rugged New England Marlboro man. He is married, there is sexual tension. Murder ensues.<br /><br />This volume is the first in a series of "Rev. Clare" books. I liked it enough to read the second one. I must admit that I want to know if Chief Van Alstyne is going to dump his wife for the Reverend. I wonder if the author will make the wife have an affair and ask for a divorce so the Chief won't be the bad guy, but will be available, and if so how many books de we have to do the "will they or won't they dance"? I already have the second book, so I will read it and see how fast or slow this relationship is going to run, and then I may just read online reviews of the latest stories in the series to see where they are. I hate the long drawn out, they might do it this time, game. (Think Stephanie Plum)<br /><br />Edit (3 years later): The author must do a lot right, because not only have I gone on to read the 2nd book, but I've continued through the whole series, liking each successive book even more. This is definitely a series that is worth the ride!<br /><br />Edit (6 years later): It's now been long enough that I don't remember what happened in this first book, so I bought the Audible version (on sale for about $5 to suck you into the series) to take on a marathon road trip, with about 40 hours of drive time). We're halfway through the trip and the book. The narrator isn't anywhere near Rev. Clare's voice in my head, but I got used to her pretty quickly. I like the way she does the support characters a lot.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2533964733034641219">...more</a>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer5596728484029771120">Apparently, this book won all sorts of awards and got glowing reviews in several respected publications, including my hometown Washington Post. My only question is whether I read the same book as everyone else? I found this book to be predictable, tedious, poorly plotted and characterized. The main characters - there were two - were both conflicted, but their conflicts were sterotypical and the intersection of those conflicts telegraphed with every paragraph. The points of view shifted around -</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5596728484029771120">Apparently, this book won all sorts of awards and got glowing reviews in several respected publications, including my hometown Washington Post. My only question is whether I read the same book as everyone else? I found this book to be predictable, tedious, poorly plotted and characterized. The main characters - there were two - were both conflicted, but their conflicts were sterotypical and the intersection of those conflicts telegraphed with every paragraph. The points of view shifted around - something that was daring with Faulkner, but confusing with this author. Finally, everyone in the book uses the Internet, but no one - not the cops or the teenagers - has a cell telephone. One cell phone and the whole plot would have crumbled under the weight of too many serendipitous coincidences. The only thing I enjoyed in this book were the descriptions of the winter countryside - the author has clearly spent some time in the Adirondacks.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_847041858">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/847041858" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt" class="left imgcol" title="Jacob Proffitt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" alt="Jacob Proffitt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/847041858?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 03, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt" class="user" title="Jacob Proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer847041858">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12836910278831168022">I finished this a couple days ago (and the next three in the series) and I'm still having a hard time putting my reaction into words. As my teen daughter would say, the feels are just too big. So I'm going to do my best on this one and hope it applies to the series as a whole as much as to this specific book and keep it relatively general (because there's no way I'll be able to do this for every book in the series and I don't plan on being so detailed in future volumes).<br /><br />While the book is structu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12836910278831168022">I finished this a couple days ago (and the next three in the series) and I'm still having a hard time putting my reaction into words. As my teen daughter would say, the feels are just too big. So I'm going to do my best on this one and hope it applies to the series as a whole as much as to this specific book and keep it relatively general (because there's no way I'll be able to do this for every book in the series and I don't plan on being so detailed in future volumes).<br /><br />While the book is structured as a mystery, that's actually the weakest aspect of the novel. It's not that hard to piece the whodunit together and really, I find that I don't much care. About the mystery. What makes the book stand-out fantastic is the characters and relationships. And I don't just mean the main characters, though that's the best part.<br /><br />Clare is an Episcopalian priest in a small town in the Adirondacks. She is warm, kind, active, and caring in a way that true Christians strive to be. Which would make her cloying if she weren't so honestly and perfectly human at the same time. The members of her congregation are all fully-developed, complex people of faith as well with a realistic (in my experience, anyway) mixture of kind and venal, saints and hypocrites working together (often in a single person), sometimes overcoming their basest instincts and sometimes not. This book would stand out as one of the best depictions of an honest Christian community even if it never got to the second part of what makes it so awesome.<br /><br />Russ is the chief of police in this small town. He's a true and honest servant of his people, working to keep peace in a town fallen on hard times and with a hearty mixture of the desperate and the priveleged—a potentially explosive combination. He has integrity in spades and an honest devotion to the law and doing what's right. He's also heavily married.<br /><br />Clare and Russ are the highlight of the book as their relationship grows from honest trust and respect (with minor, uh, and major, bumps along the way) to something... more. By the end, it is absolutely heartbreaking as Russ and Clare become aware of what the reader has suspected for some time—that they are perfectly matched, almost made for each other and that they have no way of doing anything about it without breaking both of them into something less than they are now. The poignancy of this is heartbreaking in its tragedy and purity and humanity.<br /><br />Which makes it seem like the book would be heavy. But that's the genius of Julia Spencer-Fleming—she manages to pull off that powerful emotional impact without losing the hope that lies at the heart of faith and integrity. It is easy to forget that Christianity is, at heart, a faith for the fallen and that its promise isn't ease or success or protection from harm but rather comfort in affliction and the eventual achievement of grace. Infusing a hint of grace into the promise of heartbreak (and making both real and powerful) is an amazing achievement and I am so happy to have found it in this story.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12836910278831168022">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_186218149">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186218149" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1471504-kathleen-valentine" class="left imgcol" title="Kathleen Valentine"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442476724p2/1471504.jpg" alt="Kathleen Valentine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/186218149?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 21, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1471504-kathleen-valentine" class="user" title="Kathleen Valentine">Kathleen Valentine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer186218149">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15788125858987439513"><strong>Clever Murder Mystery or Cheesy Romance Novel? You Decide.</strong><br /><br />Because it is so hot right now I got this bright idea to cool things off by reading a book that had a very chilly setting. I'd read good things about Julia Spencer-Fleming's <a title="In the Bleak Midwinter (Rev. Clare Fergusson, #1) by Julia Spencer-Fleming" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113002.In_the_Bleak_Midwinter__Rev__Clare_Fergusson___1_">In The Bleak Midwinter</a> and, since I had a copy handy, I decided to give it a read.<br /><br />As a murder mystery it is pretty good, clever, well-paced – I didn't figure it out prematurely. The setting, in the Adirondacks in winter, was excellent, the writing was good, the plot m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15788125858987439513"><strong>Clever Murder Mystery or Cheesy Romance Novel? You Decide.</strong><br /><br />Because it is so hot right now I got this bright idea to cool things off by reading a book that had a very chilly setting. I'd read good things about Julia Spencer-Fleming's <a title="In the Bleak Midwinter (Rev. Clare Fergusson, #1) by Julia Spencer-Fleming" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113002.In_the_Bleak_Midwinter__Rev__Clare_Fergusson___1_">In The Bleak Midwinter</a> and, since I had a copy handy, I decided to give it a read.<br /><br />As a murder mystery it is pretty good, clever, well-paced – I didn't figure it out prematurely. The setting, in the Adirondacks in winter, was excellent, the writing was good, the plot moved along. I very, very much liked the charcter of Russ Van Alstyne, the local sheriff. He was charming and smart and had a nice balance of brains and bluff. There were some interesting, sympathetic minor characters.... and then there was Clare Fergusson. Excuse me The Reverend Clare Fergusson, the town's new Anglican priest. Former military helicopter pilot, gourmet cook, wise-cracking smart-mouth who wears cool clothes (when not in her clericals), listens to cool music, drives a very, very cool car, and is a tough don't-mess-with-me cookie.<br /><br />In my frequent rants about annoying heroines in romance – and other – novels, I have often complained about the three things that can cause me to heave the book at a wall:<br />1. the scene where the hero <em>just happens</em> to see the heroine dancing (for sheer joy) without her knowledge and decides she is just too adorable.<br />2. the scene where the hero says or does something relatively innocuous and the heroine takes umbrage and stomps off in high dudgeon like a spoiled brat.<br />3. the scene where the heroine does something ridiculously impulsive that no woman in her right mind would do thus putting herself in peril so that the hero has to rescue her and make everything all right (and notice how cute and vulnerable she is in the process.)<br /><br />Sad to say, Reverend Clare, the Episcopal priest, does all three. One I could have handled but all three??? <br /><br />One night good old Russ (who is a married man, by the way) stops by the rectory and, through the kitchen door, just happens to witness the Rev. Clare, in a cut-off sweatshirt, dancing while she whips up a gourmet meal – which she subsequently feeds him. A few scenes later the Rev. Clare gets her patrician nose out of joint because she thinks Russ was being rude and she stomps out into the snowy night in her adorable designer suede boots and leather bomber jacket and stomps all the way back to the rectory, refusing Russ's offer for a ride when he followers her. And finally, after a torturous ride back from Albany, worrying all the way about her adorable little sports car in the on-coming blizzard, the Rev. Clare finds a mysterious message for her to meet someone at a cabin deep in the woods (in an area she has never been to) and, instantly, jumps into said adorable sports car and zooms off to the rescue. Luckily, good old <s>Dudley Dooright</s> Russ finds out in time and comes to the rescue – which gives him the opportunity to get her out of her flimsy, ice-caked clothes. Sigh.<br /><br />Look, this was a good story and there were some good characters in it and, for the most part, I liked it. I will even go so far as to say that if Clare had been a social worker or a new cop or a teacher or anything else, I might have liked her a little better. But a priest??? Yes, I know priests are people, too – heaven knows I just wrote a book about an all-too-human priest. What really bothered me about it was that, other than going to parish meetings, saying a few prayers here and there, and mentions of services she was officiating at, this priest had not the faintest evidence of any level of spirituality. Consequently, every mention of her “priesthood” might as well have had blinking letters that read “gimmick, gimmick, gimmick.”<br /><br />Obviously people like these books as there are more in the series. Chances are I might even read another one myself but when are genre writers going to stop concocting these formula-driven, ridiculous, insult-to-womanhood characters?<br /><br />As a mystery, I give this book a 4. As a romance, I give it a 2. So I'm splitting the difference with a 3 – because I like Russ. But I think he's headed down a dangerous slope and I don't think the local priest is going to help him avoid any more near-occasions-of-sin.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15788125858987439513">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2514134467781530096">Goodreads let me down on this one. I was at a loss as to what to read next so I turned to the reviews here. I didn't hate this book but I almost did. The characters were almost interesting and the plot was almost gripping. It needed to be a lot shorter and it easily could have been if you'd cut out all the details about the curtain swags, and people crossing and uncrossing their arms, and standing up and sitting down, or lord help me "swiping whip cream off his mustache."   <span style="display:none" id="freeText2514134467781530096">Goodreads let me down on this one. I was at a loss as to what to read next so I turned to the reviews here. I didn't hate this book but I almost did. The characters were almost interesting and the plot was almost gripping. It needed to be a lot shorter and it easily could have been if you'd cut out all the details about the curtain swags, and people crossing and uncrossing their arms, and standing up and sitting down, or lord help me "swiping whip cream off his mustache." I get that these details were supposed to add richness and in a deft hand they may have but here they felt pounded in by some well-meaning editor. Also, the female main character was supposed to be this amazingly well-trained ex-military person but she couldn't even figure out that she should take a quick trip to Target and pick up a decent pair of boots when it was snowing a freezing outside. Just too dumb for me. When she kept getting caught in her "thin leather boots" in horrible situations snow-falling situations, I had had enough.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5591829360202085376">Hey, I liked this! I don’t like many traditional mysteries. Though to be fair, I don’t actually like this mystery qua mystery.<br /><br />He’s the police chief of a tiny, upstate New York town. She’s a former army pilot turned Episcopal priest.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5591829360202085376">Hey, I liked this! I don’t like many traditional mysteries. Though to be fair, I don’t actually like this mystery qua mystery.<br /><br />He’s the police chief of a tiny, upstate New York town. She’s a former army pilot turned Episcopal priest. (She’s improbable in that way that makes a character seem more real, instead of less, if you know what I mean). They solve crime, yeah, whatever. But mostly they have this slow-blooming connection. This book is about them becoming friends in this wonderful, organic, completely believable way. They are sexually neutralized to each other – he’s married and she’s a priest – so they come together free from most of the usual romance bullshit. Just two interesting, conflicted, smart, ethical people who don’t notice that they’re falling until it’s way too late.<br /><br />Really nice.<br /></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1119697370">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2133686896872132448">Part way through the book I was certain I'd found a new favorite series. Then, around page 100, I figured out who the killer was. This isn't a deal-breaker - I usually identify the killer, but sometimes the how and why of it keeps me riveted. Not so here, because that's obvious too. To make matters worse, the main character, the Reverend, convinced of her own righteousness, jumps into one stupid situation after another with little thought to consequences. I cared for the other main character eve</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2133686896872132448">Part way through the book I was certain I'd found a new favorite series. Then, around page 100, I figured out who the killer was. This isn't a deal-breaker - I usually identify the killer, but sometimes the how and why of it keeps me riveted. Not so here, because that's obvious too. To make matters worse, the main character, the Reverend, convinced of her own righteousness, jumps into one stupid situation after another with little thought to consequences. I cared for the other main character even less, because I hadn't much faith in his ability to solve anything, which he ultimately proved. <br /><br />Even forgetting the fact that there was a pastor who was out there doing amateur detecting while privy to everything the police knew, there were so many things that bothered me about the procedure. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[I don't care how understaffed you are, why would your entire legwork consist of showing pictures of the dead girl at one(!) church? This, while someone on your staff goes deer hunting. Why would you voluntarily give out information to a teenager that the murdered girl was pregnant, and that you think her ex-lover was responsible? And then not confront the ex-lover immediately? The chief even takes a leisure day in between to drive his wife somewhere. And why would the cops not go to wherever it was she worked before going to college to check if they knew anything of her mystery lover? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Well, I had hopes. My library doesn't stock the rest of the series, which is probably just as well.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_24940436">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24940436" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/113980-trin" class="left imgcol" title="Trin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1181029461p2/113980.jpg" alt="Trin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/24940436?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 02, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/113980-trin" class="user" title="Trin">Trin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=american-lit" class="actionLinkLite">american-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer24940436">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7311378244382024310">Mystery in which a male cop and a female (Episcopalian) priest in a small upstate New York town team up to fight crime! I liked this more than I expected to. Russ (the cop) and Clare (the priest) are both complex, realistic characters, and I really enjoyed how the relationship between them was developed. The way they find common ground and begin to seek out and crave each other’s company felt very natural and wonderfully genderless, if you know what I mean, and after reading a lot of crappy, wei</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7311378244382024310">Mystery in which a male cop and a female (Episcopalian) priest in a small upstate New York town team up to fight crime! I liked this more than I expected to. Russ (the cop) and Clare (the priest) are both complex, realistic characters, and I really enjoyed how the relationship between them was developed. The way they find common ground and begin to seek out and crave each other’s company felt very natural and wonderfully genderless, if you know what I mean, and after reading a lot of crappy, weirdly misogynistic romance novels, it was very refreshing to see two people become attracted to each other <em>as people</em>. They solve the crime at the novel’s center based on a combination of their respective skills, and I really liked all the scenes where they just…enjoy each other’s competence. The sexual tension is well drawn out in general; Spencer-Fleming makes good use of Russ’ (and possibly her readers’) ignorance about various denominational differences in a fun scene where Russ discovers that no, Clare has not, in fact, taken a vow of celibacy—though that doesn’t change the fact that Russ is married. UST FTW!<br /><br />As for the mystery plot itself, aside from one “I’ll just follow the instructions in this telephone message of dubious origin and go out to a cabin in the middle of the woods by myself in a snowstorm without telling anyone” moment, which actually had me sending keyboard-mashing IMs to Siria, there aren’t too many bad mystery clichés or examples of terminal character stupidity. Overall, I really enjoyed it, and look forward to reading the next book in the series when my mood rolls around that way again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7311378244382024310">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2879183477147037127">Wow, this was really good! The mystery kept me guessing, yes, and I really enjoyed seeing Clare doing her priestly duties--I love stories in which religious people are portrayed as not crazy or venal or misguided. There's a good tension between Russ as the hard-headed, cynical cop and Clare as the more optimistic, generous priest, especially since neither of them is stereotypically so. But what I loved was the developing relationship between Russ and Clare, how I could see where it was going eve</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2879183477147037127">Wow, this was really good! The mystery kept me guessing, yes, and I really enjoyed seeing Clare doing her priestly duties--I love stories in which religious people are portrayed as not crazy or venal or misguided. There's a good tension between Russ as the hard-headed, cynical cop and Clare as the more optimistic, generous priest, especially since neither of them is stereotypically so. But what I loved was the developing relationship between Russ and Clare, how I could see where it was going even though they couldn't. It's interesting that Russ's wife Linda was only present in her absence, only appeared off-stage. It suggests that Russ and Linda have drifted apart, and that they don't have a lot in common (and may never have had) but not that their marriage is irredeemable or that this justifies any feelings that might be developing between Clare and Russ. I'm definitely looking forward to the rest of the series.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_808901658">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/808901658" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1145657-hallie" class="left imgcol" title="Hallie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1244842998p2/1145657.jpg" alt="Hallie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/808901658?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1145657-hallie" class="user" title="Hallie">Hallie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer808901658">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1847368580500830359">This was the perfect way to pass some hours the other day, when I needed something to take my mind off <em>things</em> and could curl up on the sofa with the dog, book and tea while the storm blew in and I was away from my world. (Our storm was wind and rain, not snow!) I really liked both the main characters, and even if the mystery wasn't brilliant, it was good enough to keep me engaged when I was so taken with Clare and Russ. I'm not sure how Clare would have seemed to someone not brought up Anglican,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1847368580500830359">This was the perfect way to pass some hours the other day, when I needed something to take my mind off <em>things</em> and could curl up on the sofa with the dog, book and tea while the storm blew in and I was away from my world. (Our storm was wind and rain, not snow!) I really liked both the main characters, and even if the mystery wasn't brilliant, it was good enough to keep me engaged when I was so taken with Clare and Russ. I'm not sure how Clare would have seemed to someone not brought up Anglican, as a lot of the humour would doubtless work (Russ is utterly clueless about Episcopalians, Roman Catholics and the differences between them), but the recognition of faults (some of the very self-satisfied, wealthy, lacking-in-compassion parishioners were sadly familiar) and strengths (Clare's deep faith, which she has no need to shove down anyone's throat, and her ability to be with people who are suffering), was a part of the good reading experience for me.<br /><br />In almost any other mystery I'd have had very stern words indeed to say about some of Clare's behaviour, but I was happy to give it a pass here, because it always made sense when considered in light of her feelings of <em>pastoral</em> responsibility. If she were helping the police in any kind of official capacity (other than the priestly office, of course!), her actions would often have been far into TSTL territory. Other readers might not give her that ministerial pass, and in that case, the whole thing might fall more than a bit flat. I did have other quibbles, like her unpreparedness for Real Winter, which was overdone for plot purposes, but nothing too serious. <br /><br />And finally - that "attraction to each other" mentioned in the blurb worried me a bit, as Russ is married. And no amount of setting his wife up as the classic "my wife doesn't understand me" (about which he and Clare even joke) would make it okay for them to go beyond friendship. I loved the last page's quiet acknowledgment of the temptation and refusal to give in to it and very much hope that somewhere along the series line, <em>something</em> will take Russ's wife off to pastures greener. I'm looking forward to reading more to find out, and willing to take the chance I'll just be teased by the hope for book after book after book...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1847368580500830359">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1030634731">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1030634731" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8319448-pat" class="left imgcol" title="Pat"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1339326250p2/8319448.jpg" alt="Pat" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1030634731?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 24, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8319448-pat" class="user" title="Pat">Pat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8319448-pat?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1030634731">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12481367703318541597">This is 3.5 stars. <br /><br /> If the measure of a successful mystery is its ability to catch and hold the reader's interest, than this book succeeds. But in order to rise about the common 'read', it should introduce a memorable and complex protagonist whose personality shows change (preferably growth) resulting from the progression of plot, interactions with subordinating characters, and self examination. Primary characters work better if I can identify or sympathize with them, although we do not have to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12481367703318541597">This is 3.5 stars. <br /><br /> If the measure of a successful mystery is its ability to catch and hold the reader's interest, than this book succeeds. But in order to rise about the common 'read', it should introduce a memorable and complex protagonist whose personality shows change (preferably growth) resulting from the progression of plot, interactions with subordinating characters, and self examination. Primary characters work better if I can identify or sympathize with them, although we do not have to share the same belief systems. <br /><br />Reading straight through, I found fluidity with pacing, character development, and plot, and, I am embarrassed to say, I failed to discover the perpetrator until the author intended. <br /><br />For me, the main strength of the novel lies in the inventive juxtaposition of an optimistic-empathetic-female-Episcopalian priest with a pessimistic-realist-police-chief, as it allows the author to visit criminology and sociology from two different perspectives. The assumption is that by the end of the novel each viewpoint will have migrated towards the other and much of the story's worth rests within that context. It also sets up the future conflict and exploration in a series...which is precisely why I intend to read more in the series. If she succeeds as she's begun, it will probably be the strongest recommendation for her well-written work. <br /><br />This is not to say there aren't little things that irritate me with the book. The major 'minor' irritation arises from her priest detective's naive and misguided insistence on going where angels fear to tread. I hope for the sake of believability, in future works this is one aspect of her personality that shows 'growth.'<br /><br />I cannot help but notice that the ratings for this series increase with each novel...and the slightly antagonistic interaction between the primary characters may well be the reason. As for me, I have been seduced by the ease and fluidity of her prose, the setting, the characters and the creative manipulation of the primaries relationship. <br /><br />On to the next novel in the series!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12481367703318541597">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6157970-in-the-bleak-midwinter" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who loves well-written books with great characters.</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=series-ongoing" class="actionLinkLite">series-ongoing</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=like-a-virgin" class="actionLinkLite">like-a-virgin</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=oh-god" class="actionLinkLite">oh-god</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=murder-was-the-case" class="actionLinkLite">murder-was-the-case</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=mystery-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=kindle-purchase-freebies" class="actionLinkLite">kindle-purchase-freebies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=female-lead-i-love" class="actionLinkLite">female-lead-i-love</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=five-%E2%98%85%E2%98%85%E2%98%85%E2%98%85%E2%98%85" class="actionLinkLite">five-?????</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=read-multiple-times" class="actionLinkLite">read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=male-lead-i-love" class="actionLinkLite">male-lead-i-love</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=recommendations-for-you" class="actionLinkLite">recommendations-for-you</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=authors-being-awesome" class="actionLinkLite">authors-being-awesome</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4847205-alicia-is-beyond-tired-of-your-ish?shelf=profession-law-enforcement-agents" class="actionLinkLite">profession-law-enforcement-agents</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer156889816">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer579809449863932779">I have read this book twice now within six months. It only got better upon the second reading. <br /><br />The story wasn't what I thought it was going to be from the blurb because of their relationship statuses in the book. So it had me worried for a very long time. I think that was the reason for the four stars I gave the book after the first time I read it. I'm going to try to keep this review to the first book alone, though it's hard as I want to comment on what comes later. I apologize if I fail at it,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText579809449863932779">I have read this book twice now within six months. It only got better upon the second reading. <br /><br />The story wasn't what I thought it was going to be from the blurb because of their relationship statuses in the book. So it had me worried for a very long time. I think that was the reason for the four stars I gave the book after the first time I read it. I'm going to try to keep this review to the first book alone, though it's hard as I want to comment on what comes later. I apologize if I fail at it, but there won't be any spoilers.<br /><br />I love Julia Spencer-Fleming's writing style. It is descriptive without being over-flowery. There are no lines that stand out as trying too hard, she has a very consistent voice. She sets scenes that draw you into what's happening in an almost effortless way. It can dip into a bit of the cliche, but it never really dives in. Fleming doesn't write a mystery that drops clues along the way, allowing the reader to play junior detective along with the characters. You get the information as the characters do and it's a snaking vine that keeps you guessing but never allows you to get it right. I'm sure some people will hate that because they love trying to put clues together, but I really liked not being bored with the mystery because it was so easy to tell whodunit. <br /><br />The story is engrossing, and there are definitely a few edge of your seat moments. One that happens on a snowy mountain that I just love. Though this scene and the climatic ending do veer somewhat into head scratching territory it's easy to forgive because they're so absorbing. <br /><br />The number one thing Fleming does best is characters. I'm a character driven person. I can forgive a lot of things in a story if I love the characters, and a decent story will be terrible to me if I hate the characters. The love I have for this series is very much tied to my love for Russ Van Alstyne and Clare Fergusson. Both are very strong characters, intelligent, with great senses of humor. They're both stubborn (and that trait definitely gets her into trouble) and can set each other off, but they also listen to each other well (most of the time). I love that they're not perfect. They don't always make the right choices (and the choices they have to make get harder and harder). You would think that would be the case with a priest, but she has to fight her pride, her stubbornness, her emotions, and temptation. She has to question herself and her calling. The two have some similarities but they are also very different. For instance, Russ is clear about being an atheist and Clare is an Episcopalian priest. They certainly have their theological discussions but he doesn't really impugn her beliefs and she never preaches at anyone who doesn't ask her to. That's another thing I love so much about her. Throughout the series I found myself wishing they were real and my friends too many times to count.<br /><br />Their friendship is so effortless and such a joy to read. They get each other on such a fundamental level. And the reader gets to <em>see</em> that! It is so rare now that a reader gets to actually see a relationship begin and unfold instead of being told that it happened. We're given many conversations, joking around and even arguments. I never feel as though I have to take anything about them on faith. We can even see when it begins to evolve into something more. It was fun picking up on things I didn't notice before the second time I read it. Almost everything about their friendship just makes me happy. I start to flail and then I end up a lot like this guy:<br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/243541.gif" /><br /><br />The secondary characters are just as easily likable, or they can be annoying or rage inducing, but that's their purpose and they're always well drawn and compelling. Even when they're doing things I don't understand.<br /><br />So, if you can't already tell from my rare, effusive gushing (that I still feel doesn't do this story justice), I heavily recommend picking up this book. Then I dare you to not devour the next six books in the series. I read all of them within a month and that was on top of reading other books, moving, and breaking bones. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="579809449863932779">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/3566415-sam" class="user" title="Sam">Sam</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer191362115">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer605509968719184912">In the Bleak Midwinter is a really great mystery. The lead character is not your typical heroine. She isn't a PI or a detective. Claire Fergusson is an Episcopal Priest. OK, she has a back ground as a former ex-Army chopper pilot, but she has given that life up and moved to Miller's Kill, New York and the care of St Alban's Church. <br /><br />When a new born infant is left on her door step before she has even had a chance to unpack, Claire finds herself thrown into the middle if church politics and the tow</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText605509968719184912">In the Bleak Midwinter is a really great mystery. The lead character is not your typical heroine. She isn't a PI or a detective. Claire Fergusson is an Episcopal Priest. OK, she has a back ground as a former ex-Army chopper pilot, but she has given that life up and moved to Miller's Kill, New York and the care of St Alban's Church. <br /><br />When a new born infant is left on her door step before she has even had a chance to unpack, Claire finds herself thrown into the middle if church politics and the towns underbelly, all while trying to find the babies mother. Right there to help her navigate is the town's police chief, Russ Van Alstyne. Russ is a good man, and helps Claire out of a few jams as she adjusts to life in the north and learns the ropes of her new town. While navigating these new paths Clair and Russ develop an attraction to each other, they find the babies mother and…they find murder.<br /><br />It’s a race to the end and man can you feel the cold. Spencer-Fleming writes a good mystery with unique and likable main characters, you want to know more about.<br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer52260076">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8197027613947827019">I'm not sure why I bought this. Someone somewhere wrote a review that intrigued me. (here on Goodreads? Can't remember now, sorry!) There's no way reading the cover would have pulled me in. A mystery - nah, not in the mood right now. Ex-military priest and ex-military cop? Sounds way too testosterone-inflated for my taste. Sleepy small town with dark undercurrents? Sounds trite. <br /><br />But what I do love is having my expectations turned upside down, and this book definitely is nothing like you would ex</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8197027613947827019">I'm not sure why I bought this. Someone somewhere wrote a review that intrigued me. (here on Goodreads? Can't remember now, sorry!) There's no way reading the cover would have pulled me in. A mystery - nah, not in the mood right now. Ex-military priest and ex-military cop? Sounds way too testosterone-inflated for my taste. Sleepy small town with dark undercurrents? Sounds trite. <br /><br />But what I do love is having my expectations turned upside down, and this book definitely is nothing like you would expect from the cover copy. I liked the sense of place, the atmosphere, the characters, and the dialog between Clare and Russ. Clare is very compelling to me. I'm looking forward to reading the next book to spend more time with her.<br /><br />The mystery? Well, I'm not really much of a mystery reader these days. But there were twists and turns and it all seemed to work out in a satisfying way at the end. I think be happy to read about these two even without the pile of dead bodies, though. <br /><br />Short version - high-quality genre reading. Kept me up late to finish it, and made me put everything else in my "current read" pile aside while I was engrossed.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer31552113">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11383286732876615065"><em>In the Bleak Midwinter </em> was better than most of the other books I've rated as 3-stars, but not quite good enough to bump it up to 4-stars. (Will we ever get 1/2 stars on GoodReads?)<br /><br />Rev. Clare Fergusson, Episcopal priest, has recently moved to the upstate New York town of Miller's Kill in the piedmont of the Adirondacks. A few weeks after her arrival, as she leaves the church after a vestry meeting on a snowy evening, she finds a newborn left on the steps of the church. The note left with the bab</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11383286732876615065"><em>In the Bleak Midwinter </em> was better than most of the other books I've rated as 3-stars, but not quite good enough to bump it up to 4-stars. (Will we ever get 1/2 stars on GoodReads?)<br /><br />Rev. Clare Fergusson, Episcopal priest, has recently moved to the upstate New York town of Miller's Kill in the piedmont of the Adirondacks. A few weeks after her arrival, as she leaves the church after a vestry meeting on a snowy evening, she finds a newborn left on the steps of the church. The note left with the baby asks that he be given to a couple, both lawyers, who are members of St. Albans. As a result of this situation, Clare meets and begins her friendship with Russ Van Alstyne, the local chief of police. While Clare and Russ try to solve the mystery of who the baby's parents are, Russ tries to help the native Virginian adapt to her first northern winter. Soon enough the pair identifies the baby's mother - a murder victim they discover in a local park. So, now they have another mystery to solve. They're still looking for the baby's father and now they are looking for the mother's murderer.<br /><br />The plot moved along nicely, but there really were no big surprises. As with many first-in-series books, the character development and establishing the relationships between the main characters were more prominent than the storyline. I was pleasantly surprised with the way the author portrayed Clare and Russ. Although she is a member of the clergy, Clare is not a meek and mild do-gooder. Before her calling to the priesthood she was an Army helicopter pilot. Russ - an avowed non-believer - is also ex-Army, returning to his hometown after a career as an MP. Religion is an important aspect of the book, as you would expect given that Clare is a priest, but it is not the focus of the book and it feels authentic. Russ's agnostic leanings provide a counterbalance for Clare's faith.<br /><br />I originally had this on my "cozy" mystery bookshelf. I mean, the main character is a female priest. It's got to be cozy, right? Wrong. Clare showed us that she can certainly stand up for herself (and others) - physically, if necessary. I'll be adding Julia Spencer-Fleming's second Rev. Clare Fergusson and Russ Van Alstyne installment to my no "next-in-series" bookshelf for future reading.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11383286732876615065">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_99308961">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99308961" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2220862-joyce-lagow" class="left imgcol" title="Joyce Lagow"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389851374p2/2220862.jpg" alt="Joyce Lagow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/99308961?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 20, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2220862-joyce-lagow" class="user" title="Joyce Lagow">Joyce Lagow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2220862-joyce-lagow?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer99308961">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8453581883728475074">1st in the Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne series.[return][return]Miller s Kill, a village in upstate New York near Lake George, is the improbable setting for this imaginative series starring an ex-Army helicopter pilot turned Epsicopal priest, Clare Fergusson, and the Chief of Police Russ Van Alstyne. A small town that lives largely off the tourist trade, Miller s Kill should be both sleepy and crime-free. In reality, like most small towns, it s neither, but certainly one doesn t expect the in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8453581883728475074">1st in the Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne series.[return][return]Miller s Kill, a village in upstate New York near Lake George, is the improbable setting for this imaginative series starring an ex-Army helicopter pilot turned Epsicopal priest, Clare Fergusson, and the Chief of Police Russ Van Alstyne. A small town that lives largely off the tourist trade, Miller s Kill should be both sleepy and crime-free. In reality, like most small towns, it s neither, but certainly one doesn t expect the incidence of murder to be quite so high! [return][return]Fortunately for the readers of this series, it is. But it doesn t start off that way.[return][return]Reverend Clare Fergusson, the new rector of the conservative parish of St. Albans Episcopal Church in Millers Kill, is not just female she s an ex-Army helicopter pilot. She s been on the job barely one month when, after a reception in the parish hall, she leaves the church only to stumble across a box containing a newborn infant and a note requesting that the child be left with a couple who are parishioners at St. Albans. The timing and the fact that the child has not been long exposed to the effects of a cold wintry evening in November suggest that whoever abandoned it was familiar with the routine at St. Albans.[return][return]Clare and Russ strike up an easy acquaintanceship, at lest in part based on common Army experience. Neither, however, is prepared for the discovery of the body of a young woman who is most certainly the mother of the baby. She clearly has been murdered.[return][return]<em>In The Bleak Midwinter</em> is an excellent start to the series. As will be true of all the books, the title is drawn from a hymn and relates at least in part to the circumstances of the story. Clare is an effective protagonist. She is believable and very well-drawn. Ditto for Russ. They are excellent counterbalances for one another.[return][return]The writing is not spectacular but well suited to the characters, the plot and the locale. Dialogue is completely believable. Spencer-Fleming gives Clare flashes of self-deprecating humor that greatly expand her character. Russ has his own voice and his own viewpoint, which combines a solid grasp of reality, hard-headed common sense needed to police a small town such as Miller s Kill, and a reserve that is necessary to maintain the objectivity he needs. Both characters are extremely appealing. Both are human, and wind up attracted to one another even though Russ s married to a woman he loves.[return][return]Other supporting characters are good, especially the members of the vestry of St. Albans. I thought that the descriptions of the day-to-day workings and concerns of the church to be one of the high points of the book aside from its plot. The internal politics are described with an obvious affection for the process. Clare s involvement is clearly one of commitment to the message of Christ and again the common sense needed to wend her way through the human failings that exist in every congregation. Her liberalism vs the innate conservatism of her vestry is well-handled, and fun to read.[return][return]As for the plot itself: Spencer-Fleming does a superb job of building and maintaining interest and tension. The subplot of the St. Alban s couple that temporarily take over care of the baby and their fight to have permanent custody is both separate from yet well-woven into the main plot. The denouement is a gripping page-turner; I couldn t put the book down until I d finished.[return][return]A spectacular entry in the genre. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8453581883728475074">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7013003-in-the-bleak-midwinter" title="ebook 9781429909051" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4150876-alexander-inglis?shelf=amateur-detective" class="actionLinkLite">amateur-detective</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4150876-alexander-inglis?shelf=police-detective" class="actionLinkLite">police-detective</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4150876-alexander-inglis?shelf=first-novel" class="actionLinkLite">first-novel</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer179893967">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6142869344629850842">In 2003, Julia Spencer-Fleming burst on the mystery scene with <em>In The Bleak Midwinter</em>, her first novel and the first in what is now a seven novel series featuring Rev Clare Fergusson of St Alban's Episcopal Church and Millers Kill Chief of Police Russ Van Alstyne. It was widely praised and lavished with awards including the 2002 Agatha Award for Best First Novel, 2003 Dilys Award and 2003 Barry Award for Best First Novel. Set in a fictional town in the New York state's Adirondack's, with referen</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6142869344629850842">In 2003, Julia Spencer-Fleming burst on the mystery scene with <em>In The Bleak Midwinter</em>, her first novel and the first in what is now a seven novel series featuring Rev Clare Fergusson of St Alban's Episcopal Church and Millers Kill Chief of Police Russ Van Alstyne. It was widely praised and lavished with awards including the 2002 Agatha Award for Best First Novel, 2003 Dilys Award and 2003 Barry Award for Best First Novel. Set in a fictional town in the New York state's Adirondack's, with references to real places like Albany and Glen's Falls, the atmosphere is semi-rural and steeped in real history: these were the stomping grounds of the original Dutch settlements as well as waves of other immigrants in the early 1700s -- among them my own ancestors.<br /><br />Barely days after arriving to take up her post at St. Alban's, Clare is leaving the rectory on a chilly early December evening and discovers a baby abandonned on her doorstep. But who's baby? At the hospital, she meets Russ, the Chief of Police and the Burnses, a middle-aged couple intent on adoption. Soon Clare and Russ have hit it off and he takes her under his wing in a neighbourly way ... even as romantic sparks smoulder (the Chief is married, but Clare, though a minister, is eligible for marriage). In trying to track down the mother, a young woman is found murdered in a local river (or "kill" in Dutch parlance). Now the search is on for the father and suddenly various members of the congregation are involved. And it's a small town: not everything is quite as it seems ... could another murder by around the corner?<br /><br />I really liked the set-up -- although I did find the "God" bits distracting (they are expected given the premise). This is a mystery in the Agatha Christie vein: murder, a puzzle, some character development ... it's not "Christian fiction" with a hidden message or supernatural intervention. The dialogue in the first half of the book seemed quite forced in places as the author worked through the details of the back story. Delightfully, however, the book hit its paces and the pay off was a believable puzzle solved, motivations of characters credible and dialog that increasingly wore well on Clare, Russ and other key figures. No less than Charlaine Harris and Louise Penny have written appreciative blurbs on Ms Spencer-Fleming's behalf. Definitely an entertainment and a series worth exploring.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6142869344629850842">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_100811479">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100811479" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/406686-steve" class="left imgcol" title="Steve"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1292206847p2/406686.jpg" alt="Steve" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/100811479?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/406686-steve" class="user" title="Steve">Steve</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer100811479">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16131384907570727532">Winner of a half dozen awards for first novel, it’s easy to see why. Russ and Clare, the protagonists and, respectively married police chief and new Episcopal priest in Miller’s Kill, a rural New York State community, work together on a case that begins with Clare’s finding an abandoned newborn boy at the church, a couple of murders, and the solving them. Both Russ and Clare face unforeseen life-threatening dangers in taking on the case and its principals. The mystery, the child and murders, is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16131384907570727532">Winner of a half dozen awards for first novel, it’s easy to see why. Russ and Clare, the protagonists and, respectively married police chief and new Episcopal priest in Miller’s Kill, a rural New York State community, work together on a case that begins with Clare’s finding an abandoned newborn boy at the church, a couple of murders, and the solving them. Both Russ and Clare face unforeseen life-threatening dangers in taking on the case and its principals. The mystery, the child and murders, is cleverly and enjoyably weaved by Spencer-Fleming. All of that is only improved by the relationship of Russ and Clare, a friendship based largely on caring for their respective flocks, but also sustained by their increasing trust for one another and the commonality their caring and military backgrounds provides them. The townsfolk, minor characters and suspects, are well made, also. Russ and Clare are both easy to relate to and well fleshed-out characters, something enjoyable and which makes me glad to have already purchased two of their later books. I look forward to enjoying them as much as I did this one.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16131384907570727532">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer392529236830545295">I enjoyed this! It's the kind of writing that just works for me. Solid and flows well.<br /><br />I really appreciated how religious was handled in this book. I get a little nervous about the fictional portrayal of religious leaders. Sometimes it seems like fiction portrays it as just another job when ideally it should be more than that. And it WAS more than that for Clare. But I also liked that it was very clear that she was just a regular person, too. :D<br /><br />And the friendship between Clare and Russ was GREAT.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText392529236830545295">I enjoyed this! It's the kind of writing that just works for me. Solid and flows well.<br /><br />I really appreciated how religious was handled in this book. I get a little nervous about the fictional portrayal of religious leaders. Sometimes it seems like fiction portrays it as just another job when ideally it should be more than that. And it WAS more than that for Clare. But I also liked that it was very clear that she was just a regular person, too. :D<br /><br />And the friendship between Clare and Russ was GREAT. It's hard to make those kind of connections as an adult and I feel like this reflected that, that idea of "who do you talk to?" That person isn't easy to find.<br /><br />I suspect milage might vary on this, but I thought Clare's reasons for getting involved in the case made sense and I generally understood why went off on her own instead of contacting the police. <br /><br />(I did figure out who did it, but I think that's more about familiarity with this kind of story than this book in particular.)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9332718797711399428">4.5 stars, rounded up<br /><br />I loved this book. It's an excellent introduction to the characters and small town setting for this mystery series. This is a well-constructed, well-written mystery, with nuanced characters, some twists and turns in plot, and the promise of romance.<br /><br />The only thing that bugged me was the heroine jumping into danger at the drop of a hat, instead of calling her new best bud the police chief. Nevertheless, I splurged on book #2, which I heard is better than book #1. <br /><br />I have a feel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9332718797711399428">4.5 stars, rounded up<br /><br />I loved this book. It's an excellent introduction to the characters and small town setting for this mystery series. This is a well-constructed, well-written mystery, with nuanced characters, some twists and turns in plot, and the promise of romance.<br /><br />The only thing that bugged me was the heroine jumping into danger at the drop of a hat, instead of calling her new best bud the police chief. Nevertheless, I splurged on book #2, which I heard is better than book #1. <br /><br />I have a feeling I'll be digging into this entire series for a while.<br /><br /></span>
